This is one of the few songs where I can say I'm 90% sure of the meaning. It's about an assassination of some influential person. I assume a woman. And he's observing her through the scope. Noticing silly little details like the trace of body paint from the cover shoot she just left, perhaps to promote some  philanthropic cause of hers (also, cars have body paint, but I digress), and if you listen carefully you can hear him taking the shot, and see her collapse, blood flying everywhere. And, just as our sniper blends in to the rooftops, so do the lyrics camouflage a darker meaning.

I despised the new album but THIS SONG MAN. ADDICTING. I can't get enough of this song. Arctic Monkeys were in an impossible position after the release of AM because that album (not my favourite but absolutely brilliant) was unmatched in its popularity, frankly its impossible to compete with, popularity-wise. I've found that each album they released has a new sound, and you can kind of see that this wasn't a random album to release, they have been moving towards this sound little by little. I do really respect them for just going and making music that they're going to enjoy performing instead of attempting to create a second AM album. I'm going to miss the Arctic Monkeys that made Whatever People Say I Am That's What I'm Not, but you can have too much of a good thing, and if they'd stuck with it, we never would have gotten other great albums they've released. The Car isn't my cup of tea, but this band has given me plenty over the years, I was barely 1 years old when they released their debut studio album, so chances are, this is a sound I'll grow into later.

I am in awe of (and in love with) this record. It is truly inspiring to see they are constantly evolving and doing what they are passionate about. I have been a fan since 2008 and I love each of their albums for a different reason. The nostalgia I feel towards their earlier records (and for my own teenage years) will never change, but I would not have it any other way. I am here for it. As we are collectively maturing as a generation, even if our lives have almost nothing in common, I find something relatable each time they evolve. I am forever grateful for their music, it gives me something to look forward to and hold dear. I've been listening to Arctic Monkeys, ever since I was ten years old (I'm twenty-eight now). I've listened to a lot of their different sounds, through each album... observed the evolution of both the band, and Alex Turner â€” I'll admit it. I didn't like this album, when I first heard it. I thought it sounded far too similar to "Tranquility Base Hotel And Casino", when I first heard it and I felt sad that I waited four years for something so anti-climactic. I was anticipating something, that was far removed. Regardless, I've come to realize that this album is more or less the next logical step after the former â€” it seems to me, as if Alex Turner's sensibilities from his other musical projects, as well as his history are visibly coming to full circle. I see that his work is becoming more uniquely his own, and for that reason... as someone who has been listening to their work for years, I am immensely joyful. It seems more 'full', and 'balanced'... and that to me, reflects how he's evolved as an artist. I'm anticipating their, as well his (Turner's) development musically for the future. Of course, this is pure opinion from my subjective standpoint. Feel free to agree, or disagree â€” I just felt compelled to say something after the long four year wait.

Ill admit i dismissed the arctic monkeys when first heard them. It was when Florescent Adolescent was released. I remember telling my friends they were a "terrible band with a terrible name" and that they would "come and go faster than my ex". Boy was i wrong. AM released during what was probably my most formative years alongside " ..like clockwork" ... the second I heard "do i wanna know" i realized I was wrong. AM was my 2nd fav album of 2013 and became one of my top 5 of all time. I dug i to the backlog and discovered many of my curre t favorite songs. TBH&C initially disapointed me but eventually i remembered my claim that the band may well be the bealtes of my generation and accepted and enjoyed the sound. Mirrorball and body paint have solidified my claim. We are entering prine Arctic Monkeys.... the songs they release from now on will be remembered for generations the same way we all remember Elelanor Rigby or Sgt Pepper. This a band transitioning from childhood into adulthood. And aging quite gracefully

Nice
I feel kinda weird about this album coming up.  Both songs so far have been good-to-great (imo), and you have to judge things for what they are rather than what you want them to be. In that regard, I'm happy Alex is making the music he feels best prepared to make.    But...I feel like for a band that famously kept things moving, it feels like Alex is a little stuck in an era, between this, TBHC & TLSP2. Don't get me wrong, there's obviously some difference between this music and the last album....but it doesn't really pack a surprise, does it? We all would've predicted more longe-y grandiose music with less hooks. And given it's been over 5 years since TBHC, I kinda feel glum about that lack of change.  I guess this is where Alex goes from here on out, and all our dads will be onboard with it. To me, it signals losing their 'edge' (i wasn't expecting to suddenly start strumming downwards quickly again or anything, but still), but at least the quality is still real good. Certainly beats Alex making music that he's not enthused about.
